COMPRESSIVE PILE LOAD TEST  
TEST PILE (TP-4) 
FY14 MCON PROJECT P-270 
DRYDOCK WATERFRONT FACILITY 
PHNSY & IMF 
JOINT BASE PEARL HARBOR-HICKAM, OAHU, HAWAII 
Dear Mr. Placencia: 
In accordance with the project specifications, one compressive pile load test was 
conducted on a specified test pile, designated as TP-4, for the MCON Project P-270 
Drydock Waterfront Facility between January 28 and 30, 2015.  This letter report presents 
the results of our field observations and the test data obtained during the pile load test. 
The compressive pile load test was conducted on a 24-inch octagonal precast, 
prestressed concrete pile.  Based on the project specifications, Test Pile TP-4 was cast 
with a length of 81.6 feet and instrumented with 12 vibrating wire embedment strain gages 
(Model No. VCE-4200) manufactured by Geokon.  The embedment strain gages were 
installed in pairs at levels spaced at about 15 feet along the load test pile, with the first 
level at about 3 feet above the tip of the pile. The test pile was driven to a depth of about 
61.5 feet below the existing ground surface, which corresponds to a pile tip elevation of 
about -53.8 feet MSL.  The approximate location of the load test pile is shown on the Test 
Pile Location Plan, Plate 1.   
At the completion of initial pile driving, Test Pile TP-4 was sticking up approximately 
20 feet above the existing ground surface, resulting in two levels of strain gages above the 
ground surface. To accommodate the compressive pile load test setup and testing frame, 
the top 18 feet of the pile stickup above the ground surface was cutoff, resulting in the loss 
of four strain gages (two levels), designated as SG-1 through SG-4.  Strain gage locations 
within the concrete pile and the final depths below the ground surface after pile driving are 
shown in the following table. 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc.

Test Pile TP-4 was driven on January 10, 2015.  The test pile was driven using a 
Delmag D30-23 hammer delivering a maximum rated energy of 66,100 foot-pounds.  
During the test pile driving, a Geotechnical Quality Control Specialist maintained a record 
of the blow counts and field observations of the driving behavior.  The test pile driving log 
is presented as Plate 2. 
Test Pile TP-4 was driven to an elevation of about -53.8 feet MSL.  The test pile 
was driven to a depth where approximately 20 feet of the pile was left above the ground 
surface.  The top 18 feet of concrete was chipped off in order to provide sufficient space to 
fit the load testing frame.  Therefore, the total length of the load test pile was 63.5 feet 
measured from the top to the tip of the test pile.  A multiplexer was used to connect the 
eight embedment strain gages to a Geokon Micro-10 datalogger, which recorded the 
strains in the embedment strain gages during the compressive pile load test. 
The test pile was loaded in general accordance with ASTM D 1143/1143M 
Procedure B – Maintained test procedure.  Test Pile TP-4 was gradually loaded to a 
maximum test load of 450 kips in increment of 50 kips.  Each load increment was held at 
least 30 minutes or until the rate of movement less than 0.01 inch per hour.  The maximum 
test load was maintained for at least 12 hours while the rate of movement was less than 
0.01 inch per hour, otherwise it should be held for 24 hours. 
Subsequently, the test load was unloaded in four decrements.  Each unload 
decrement was held for about an hour.  The final rebound reading was taken 12 hours 
after the test load had been removed.  Two dial gauges supported on two reference 
beams and two wire lines with mirrors and scales installed on opposite sides of the test 
pile were used to measure pile head displacement.  The reference beams were also 
independently checked for potential movement during the test by scales and level 
surveying.  The load test readings and the load-displacement curve are presented on 
Plates 3 and 4, respectively.  The compressive pile load test results are summarized as 
follows. 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc.

Based on the shape of the curve of the compressive load test and the Davisson 
failure criteria, the 24-inch octagonal concrete pile did not fail at the maximum 
compressive test load of about 450 kips.  The strain changes in the eight embedment 
strain gages were recorded using a Micro-10 datalogger during the compressive pile load 
test.  The data was downloaded and converted into a Microsoft Excel file.  The printout of 
the strain gage readings are presented in Appendix A.  The electronic version of the strain 
data (Excel format) will be transmitted via e-mail. 
It should be noted that the load test was not setup in full conformance with 
ASTM D1143/D1143M, as described below, due to the physical constraint of the site 
access. 
1. 
The clear distance between the edge of the load frame cribbing and face of 
the test pile is 3 feet. The specifications require a clear distance of at least 
5 feet. 
2. 
The clear distance between the edge of the cribbing and reference beam 
supports is about 2 feet. The specifications require at least 8 feet of clear 
distance.  
To mitigate the concern of the ground settlement affecting the static load test 
system, an independent measurement system was utilized in addition to the dial gages 
and piano wires with mirror readings.  Settlement measurement of the test pile during 
loading was measured from the reference beams.  The reference beams were also 
measured for vertical movement, using the independent engineering level, during the load 
testing.  The measurement did not indicate ground settlement during the load testing.  
Based on the results of the measurements and loading curves, we believe the 
non-conforming items did not result in adverse effects of the load test results.  
General information pertaining to the embedment strain gages, calibration sheet for 
the strain gages, and calibration sheet for the load cell are included in Appendix B. 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc. Page 4

Strain Gage Type Nominal Batch Factor (B)
Model 4000

Model 4200
Please Note: To calculate changes of strain use the formula Au= (R1-R0)G x B
where G is the gage factor for that particular model of strain gage.
This applies only to dataloggers
Where the strains are read using GK403 or GK404 readout boxes on the appropriate channels C, D or
E, the displayed readings already include the gage factor ,G, so that with portable readout boxes the
change of strain is simply (R1-RO) x B microstrain
